			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">House of Hohenzollern</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>House of Hohenzollern</b> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Standard_German" title="Help:IPA/Standard German">[ˈhoːənˈʦɔlɐn]</a></span> is a <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">dynasty</a> of former princes, <a href="/wiki/Prince-elector" title="Prince-elector">electors</a>, kings and emperors of <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Prussia</a>, the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a>. The family arose in the area around the town of <a href="/wiki/Hechingen" title="Hechingen">Hechingen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabia</a> during the 11th century and took their name from <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The first ancestor of the Hohenzollerns was mentioned in 1061.</p>
<p>The Hohenzollern family split into two branches, the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Swabia" title="Swabia">Swabian</a> branch and the <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg#List_of_burgraves" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Franconian branch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup> which later became the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussian</a> branch. The Swabian branch ruled the principalities of <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Hechingen" title="Hohenzollern-Hechingen">Hohenzollern-Hechingen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> until 1849, and also ruled <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Romania" title="Kingdom of Romania">Romania</a> from 1866 to 1947. Members of the Franconian branch became <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margrave of Brandenburg</a> in 1415 and <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duke of Prussia</a> in 1525.</p>
<p>The Margraviate of Brandenburg and the Duchy of Prussia were ruled in <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a> after 1618 and were called Brandenburg-Prussia. The <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a> was created in 1701, eventually leading to the <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">unification of Germany</a> and the creation of the German Empire in 1871, with the Hohenzollerns as hereditary <a href="/wiki/German_Emperor" title="German Emperor">German Emperors</a> and Kings of Prussia.</p>
<p>Germany's defeat in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in 1918 led to the <a href="/wiki/German_Revolution_of_1918%E2%80%9319" title="German Revolution of 1918–19">German Revolution</a>. The Hohenzollerns were overthrown and the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> was established, thus bringing an end to the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Germany" title="Monarchy of Germany">German monarchy</a>. <a href="/wiki/Georg_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Prussia" title="Georg Friedrich, Prince of Prussia">Georg Friedrich, Prince of Prussia</a> is the current head of the royal Prussian line, while <a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern</a> is the head of the princely Swabian line.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-28"><a href="#Palaces_of_the_Prussian_Hohenzollerns"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Palaces of the Prussian Hohenzollerns</span></a></li>
<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-29"><a href="#Palaces_of_the_Frankonian_branches"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Palaces of the Frankonian branches</span></a></li>

<ul>

</ul>
</li>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="County_of_Zollern">County of Zollern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: County of Zollern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg/220px-Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg/330px-Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg/440px-Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3504" data-file-height="2336" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Burg_Hohenzollern_ak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a> near <a href="/wiki/Hechingen" title="Hechingen">Hechingen</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg/170px-Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg" width="170" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg/255px-Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg/340px-Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="417" data-file-height="591" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alpirsbach_Kloster_Kirche_innen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Alpirsbach_Abbey" title="Alpirsbach Abbey">Alpirsbach Abbey</a>, founded by the Hohenzollerns.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Zollern, from 1218 Hohenzollern, was a <a href="/wiki/County" title="County">county</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. Later its capital was <a href="/wiki/Hechingen" title="Hechingen">Hechingen</a>.</p>
<p>The Hohenzollerns named their estates after <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_Jura" title="Swabian Jura">Swabian Alps</a>. The Hohenzollern Castle lies on a 855 meters high mountain called <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_(mountain)" title="Hohenzollern (mountain)">Hohenzollern</a>. It still belongs to the family today.</p>
<p>The dynasty was first mentioned in 1061. According to the medieval chronicler <a href="/wiki/Berthold_of_Reichenau" title="Berthold of Reichenau">Berthold of Reichenau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Burkhard_I,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Burkhard I, Count of Zollern">Burkhard I, Count of Zollern</a> (<i>de Zolorin</i>) was born before 1025 and died in 1061.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1095 Count Adalbert of Zollern founded the <a href="/wiki/Order_of_Saint_Benedict" title="Order of Saint Benedict">Benedictine</a> <a href="/wiki/Alpirsbach_Abbey" title="Alpirsbach Abbey">monastery of Alpirsbach</a>, situated in the <a href="/wiki/Black_Forest" title="Black Forest">Black Forest</a>.</p>
<p>The Zollerns received the <a href="/wiki/Graf" title="Graf">comital</a> title from Emperor <a href="/wiki/Henry_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry V, Holy Roman Emperor">Henry V</a> in 1111.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>As loyal vassals of the Swabian <a href="/wiki/Hohenstaufen" title="Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> dynasty, they were able to significantly enlarge their territory. Count <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick III</a> (c. 1139 – c. 1200) accompanied Emperor <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Frederick I, Holy Roman Emperor">Frederick Barbarossa</a> against <a href="/wiki/Henry_the_Lion" title="Henry the Lion">Henry the Lion</a> in 1180, and through his marriage was granted the <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgraviate of Nuremberg</a> by Emperor <a href="/wiki/Henry_VI,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Henry VI, Holy Roman Emperor">Henry VI</a> in 1192. In about 1185 he married Sophia of <a href="/wiki/Burg_Raabs_an_der_Thaya" title="Burg Raabs an der Thaya">Raabs</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Conrad_II_of_Raabs" title="Conrad II of Raabs">Conrad II</a>, Burgrave of Nuremberg.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup> After the death of Conrad II who left no male heirs, Frederick III was granted Nuremberg as <a href="/wiki/Burgrave" title="Burgrave">Burgrave</a> Frederick I.</p>
<p>In 1218 the burgraviate passed to Frederick's younger son <a href="/wiki/Conrad_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Conrad I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Conrad I</a>, he thereby became the ancestor of the <a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconian</a> Hohenzollern branch, which acquired the <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Electorate of Brandenburg</a> in 1415.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:left;"></div>
<p>Some historians in the past draw the wrong conclusion that the Hohenzollerns may have derived from the <a href="/wiki/Hunfridings" title="Hunfridings">Burchardings</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Counts_of_Zollern_(1061–1204)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Counts_of_Zollern_.281061.E2.80.931204.29">Counts of Zollern (1061–1204)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Counts of Zollern (1061–1204)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li>until 1061: <a href="/wiki/Burkhard_I,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Burkhard I, Count of Zollern">Burkhard I</a><sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li>before 1125: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick I, Count of Zollern">Frederick I</a><sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li>between ca. 1125 and 1142: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_II_of_Zollern" title="Frederick II of Zollern">Frederick II</a>, eldest son of Frederick I<sup id="cite_ref-Schmid_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmid-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:XLI</sup></li>
<li>between ca. 1143 and 1150-1155: Burkhard II, 2nd oldest son of Frederick I<sup id="cite_ref-Schmid_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmid-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:XLI</sup></li>
<li>between ca. 1150-1155 and 1160: Gotfried of Zimmern, 4th oldest son of Frederick I<sup id="cite_ref-Schmid_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schmid-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:XLI</sup></li>
<li>before 1171&#160;– c. 1200: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick III/I</a> (son of Frederick II, also <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgrave of Nuremberg</a>)</li>
</ul>
<p>After Frederick's death, his sons partitioned the family lands between themselves:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick IV, Count of Zollern">Frederick IV</a> received the county of Zollern and the burgraviate of Nuremberg in 1200 from his father, thereby founding the Swabian branch of the House of Hohenzollern. The Swabian line remains <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Conrad_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Conrad I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Conrad III</a> received the burgraviate of Nuremberg from his brother Frederick IV in 1218, thereby founding the Franconian branch of the House of Hohenzollern. Members of the Franconian line eventually became the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussian</a> branch. The Franconian line later converted to <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestantism</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franconian_branch">Franconian branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Franconian branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The cadet Franconian branch of the House of Hohenzollern was founded by Conrad I, Burgrave of Nuremberg (1186-1261).</p>
<p>The family supported the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenstaufen" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Hohenstaufen">Hohenstaufen</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">Habsburg</a> rulers of the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a> during the 12th to 15th centuries, being rewarded with several territorial grants. Beginning in the 16th century, this branch of the family became Protestant and decided on expansion through marriage and the purchase of surrounding lands.</p>
<p>In the first phase, the family gradually added to their lands, at first with many small acquisitions in the Franconian region of <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ansbach" title="Ansbach">Ansbach</a> in 1331</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kulmbach" title="Kulmbach">Kulmbach</a> in 1340</li>
</ul>
<p>In the second phase, the family expanded their lands further with large acquisitions in the Brandenburg and Prussian regions of Germany and current Poland:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a> in 1417</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duchy of Prussia</a> in 1618</li>
</ul>
<p>These acquisitions eventually transformed the Hohenzollerns from a minor German princely family into one of the most important dynasties in Europe.</p>
<h3><span id="Burgraves_of_Nuremberg_(1192–1427)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Burgraves_of_Nuremberg_.281192.E2.80.931427.29">Burgraves of Nuremberg (1192–1427)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Burgraves of Nuremberg (1192–1427)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_(Haus_Hohenzollern).svg" class="image"><img alt="COA family de Burggrafen von Nürnberg (Haus Hohenzollern).svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg/75px-COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg.png" width="75" height="82" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg/113px-COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg/150px-COA_family_de_Burggrafen_von_N%C3%BCrnberg_%28Haus_Hohenzollern%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="550" data-file-height="600" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ansbach-Bayreuth.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Ansbach-Bayreuth.png/220px-Ansbach-Bayreuth.png" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Ansbach-Bayreuth.png/330px-Ansbach-Bayreuth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/da/Ansbach-Bayreuth.png 2x" data-file-width="361" data-file-height="359" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ansbach-Bayreuth.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Region of Nuremberg, Ansbach, Kulmbach and Bayreuth (<a href="/wiki/Franconia" title="Franconia">Franconia</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgraviate of Nuremberg</a></div>
<ul>
<li>1192–1200/1204: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick I</a> (also count of Zollern as Frederick III)</li>
<li>1204–1218: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick IV, Count of Zollern">Frederick II</a> (son of, also count of Zollern as Frederick IV)</li>
<li>1218–1261/1262: <a href="/wiki/Conrad_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Conrad I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Conrad I/III</a> (brother of, also count of Zollern)</li>
<li>1262–1297: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick III, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick III</a> (c. 1220–1297), son of</li>
<li>1297–1300: <a href="/wiki/John_I,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="John I, Burgrave of Nuremberg">John I</a> (c. 1279–1300), son of</li>
<li>1300–1332: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick IV, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick IV</a> (1287–1332), brother of</li>
<li>1332–1357: <a href="/wiki/John_II,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="John II, Burgrave of Nuremberg">John II</a> (c. 1309–1357), son of</li>
<li>1357–1397: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_V,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick V, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick V</a> (before 1333–1398), son of</li>
</ul>
<p>At Frederick V's death on 21 January 1398, his lands were partitioned between his two sons:</p>
<ul>
<li>1397–1420: <a href="/wiki/John_III,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="John III, Burgrave of Nuremberg">John III/I</a> (son of, also <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Bayreuth" title="Principality of Bayreuth">Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach</a>)</li>
<li>1397–1427: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick VI/I/I</a>, (brother of, also <a href="/wiki/List_of_rulers_of_Brandenburg" title="List of rulers of Brandenburg">Elector</a> and <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margrave of Brandenburg</a>, also <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Ansbach" title="Principality of Ansbach">Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach</a> and Brandenburg.Kulmbach)</li>
</ul>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/John_III,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="John III, Burgrave of Nuremberg">John III/I</a>'s death on 11 June 1420, the margraviates of Brandenburg-Ansbach and Brandenburg-Kulmbach were briefly reunited under <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick VI/I/I</a>. He ruled the Margraviate of Brandenburg-Ansbach after 1398. From 1420, he became Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach. From 1411 Frederick VI became governor of Brandenburg and later Elector and Margrave of Brandenburg as Frederick I. Upon his death on 21 September 1440, his territories were divided among his sons:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_II,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick II, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick II, Elector of Brandenburg</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Albrecht_III_Achilles,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Albrecht III Achilles, Elector of Brandenburg">Albert III, Elector of Brandenburg and Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Kulmbach" title="John, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach">John II, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach</a></li>
</ul>
<p>In 1427 Frederick, Elector of Brandenburg sold <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Castle" title="Nuremberg Castle">Nuremberg Castle</a> and his rights as burgrave to the <a href="/wiki/Free_Imperial_City_of_Nuremberg" title="Free Imperial City of Nuremberg">Imperial City of Nuremberg</a>. The territories of Brandenburg-Ansbach and Brandenburg-Kulmbach remained possessions of the family, once parts of the Burgraviate of Nuremberg.</p>

<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px">

</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach_(1398–1791)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach_.281398.E2.80.931791.29">Margraves of Brandenburg-Ansbach (1398–1791)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Margraves of Brandenburg-Ansbach (1398–1791)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Ansbach" title="Principality of Ansbach">Principality of Ansbach</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg/75px-Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg.png" width="75" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg/113px-Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg/150px-Wappen_Brandenburg-Ansbach.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="660" /></a></div>
<ul>
<li>1398–1440: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick I</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach)</li>
<li>1440–1486: <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_III_Achilles,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Albrecht III Achilles, Elector of Brandenburg">Albert I/I/III Achilles</a> (son of, also Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach and Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1486–1415: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Frederick I, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Frederick II/II</a> (son of, also Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach)</li>
<li>1515–1543: <a href="/wiki/George,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George I/I the Pious</a> (son of, also Duke of Brandenburg-Jägerndorf)</li>
<li>1543–1603: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George Frederick I/I/I/I</a> (son of, also Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach, Duke of Brandenburg-Jägerndorf and Regent of Prussia)</li>
<li>1603–1625: <a href="/wiki/Joachim_Ernst,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Joachim Ernst, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Joachim Ernst</a> (1583–1625), son of <a href="/wiki/John_George,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="John George, Elector of Brandenburg">John George of Brandenburg</a></li>
<li>1625–1634: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_III,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Frederick III, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Frederick III</a> (1616–1634), son of</li>
<li>1634–1667: <a href="/wiki/Albert_II,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Albert II, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Albert II</a></li>
<li>1667–1686: <a href="/wiki/John_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="John Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">John Frederick</a> (1654–1686), son of</li>
<li>1686–1692: <a href="/wiki/Christian_Albert,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Christian Albert, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Christian I Albrecht</a></li>
<li>1692–1703: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick_II,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George Frederick II, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George Frederick II/II</a> (later Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach)</li>
<li>1703–1723: <a href="/wiki/William_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="William Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">William Frederick</a> (before 1686–1723), son of <a href="/wiki/John_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="John Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">John Frederick</a></li>
<li>1723–1757: <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Charles William Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Charles William</a> (1712–1757), son of</li>
<li>1757: <a href="/wiki/Charles_Alexander,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Charles Alexander, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Christian II Frederick</a> (1757–1791) (son of, also Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach)</li>
</ul>
<p>On 2 December 1791, Christian II Frederick sold the sovereignty of his principalities to King <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_II_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William II of Prussia">Frederick William II of Prussia</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Kulmbach_(1398–1604),_later_Brandenburg-Bayreuth_(1604–1791)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Kulmbach_.281398.E2.80.931604.29.2C_later_Brandenburg-Bayreuth_.281604.E2.80.931791.29">Margraves of Brandenburg-Kulmbach (1398–1604), later Brandenburg-Bayreuth (1604–1791)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Margraves of Brandenburg-Kulmbach (1398–1604), later Brandenburg-Bayreuth (1604–1791)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Bayreuth" title="Principality of Bayreuth">Principality of Bayreuth</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png" class="image"><img alt="CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png/75px-CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png" width="75" height="83" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png/113px-CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png/150px-CoA.Brand-Bayreuth.png 2x" data-file-width="545" data-file-height="600" /></a></div>
<ul>
<li>1398–1420: <a href="/wiki/John_III,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="John III, Burgrave of Nuremberg">John I</a> (c. 1369–1420), son of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_V,_Burgrave_of_Nuremberg" title="Frederick V, Burgrave of Nuremberg">Frederick V of Nuremberg</a></li>
<li>1420–1440: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick I</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach)</li>
<li>1440–1457: <a href="/wiki/John,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Kulmbach" title="John, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach">John II</a> (1406–1464), son of</li>
<li>1457–1486: <a href="/wiki/Albrecht_III_Achilles,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Albrecht III Achilles, Elector of Brandenburg">Albert I/I/III Achilles</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach and Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1486–1495: <a href="/wiki/Siegmund,_Margrave_of_Bayreuth" title="Siegmund, Margrave of Bayreuth">Siegmund</a> (1468–1495), son of</li>
<li>1495–1515: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Frederick I, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Frederick II/II</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach)</li>
<li>1515–1527: <a href="/wiki/Casimir,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Casimir, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Casimir</a> (1481–1527), son of</li>
<li>1527–1553: <a href="/wiki/Albert_Alcibiades,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Kulmbach" title="Albert Alcibiades, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach">Albert II Alcibiades</a> (1522–1557), son of</li>
<li>1553–1603: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George Frederick I/I/I/I</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach, Duke of Brandenburg-Jägerndorf and Regent of Prussia)</li>
<li>1603–1655: <a href="/wiki/Christian,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Christian, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Christian I</a> (1581–1655), son of <a href="/wiki/John_George,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="John George, Elector of Brandenburg">John George,of Brandenburg</a></li>
<li>1655–1712: <a href="/wiki/Christian_Ernst,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Christian Ernst, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Christian II Ernst</a> (1644–1712), son of <a href="/wiki/Erdmann_August_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Erdmann August of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Erdmann August</a></li>
<li>1712–1726: <a href="/wiki/George_William,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="George William, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">George I William</a> (1678–1726), son of</li>
<li>1726–1735: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick_Charles,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="George Frederick Charles, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">George Frederick II/II</a> (previously Margrave of Kulmbach)</li>
<li>1735–1763: <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Frederick IV</a> (1711–1763), son of</li>
<li>1763–1769: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Christian,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth" title="Frederick Christian, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth">Frederick V Christian</a> (1708–1769), son of <a href="/wiki/Christian_Heinrich,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Bayreuth-Kulmbach" title="Christian Heinrich, Margrave of Brandenburg-Bayreuth-Kulmbach">Christian Heinrich</a></li>
<li>1769–1791: <a href="/wiki/Charles_Alexander,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="Charles Alexander, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">Charles Alexander</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach)</li>
</ul>
<p>On 2 December 1791, Charles Alexander sold the sovereignty of his principalities to King Frederick William II of Prussia.</p>
<p>From 8 January 1701 the title of Elector of Brandenburg was attached to the title of King <i>in</i> Prussia and, from 13 September 1772, to that of King <i>of</i> Prussia.</p>
<h3><span id="Dukes_of_Jägerndorf_(1523–1622)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dukes_of_J.C3.A4gerndorf_.281523.E2.80.931622.29">Dukes of Jägerndorf (1523–1622)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Dukes of Jägerndorf (1523–1622)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Krnov" title="Duchy of Krnov">Duchy of Krnov</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Krnov_znak.png" class="image"><img alt="Krnov znak.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Krnov_znak.png/80px-Krnov_znak.png" width="80" height="104" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Krnov_znak.png/120px-Krnov_znak.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d8/Krnov_znak.png 2x" data-file-width="156" data-file-height="202" /></a></div>
<p>The Duchy of Jägerndorf (Krnov) was purchased in 1523.</p>
<ul>
<li>1541–1543: <a href="/wiki/George,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George I the Pious</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach)</li>
<li>1543–1603: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George Frederick I</a> (also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach and Regent of Prussia)</li>
<li>1603–1606: <a href="/wiki/Joachim_III_Frederick,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Joachim III Frederick, Elector of Brandenburg">Joachim I</a> (also Regent of Prussia and Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1606–1621: <a href="/wiki/Johann_Georg_von_Brandenburg" title="Johann Georg von Brandenburg">Johann Georg von Brandenburg</a></li>
</ul>
<p>The duchy of Jägerndorf was confiscated by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Ferdinand III, Holy Roman Emperor">Emperor Ferdinand III</a> in 1622.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brandenburg-Prussian_branch">Brandenburg-Prussian branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Brandenburg-Prussian branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg_(1415–1619)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg_.281415.E2.80.931619.29">Margraves of Brandenburg (1415–1619)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Margraves of Brandenburg (1415–1619)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg">Margraviate of Brandenburg</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FrederikIboek.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/FrederikIboek.jpg/220px-FrederikIboek.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/FrederikIboek.jpg/330px-FrederikIboek.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/FrederikIboek.jpg/440px-FrederikIboek.jpg 2x" data-file-width="669" data-file-height="525" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FrederikIboek.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick VI</a> became Margrave of Brandenburg in 1415.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1411 <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick I, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick VI</a>, Burgrave of Nuremberg was appointed governor of Brandenburg in order to restore order and stability. At the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Constance" title="Council of Constance">Council of Constance</a> in 1415, King <a href="/wiki/Sigismund,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Sigismund, Holy Roman Emperor">Sigismund</a> elevated Frederick to the rank of Elector and Margrave of Brandenburg as Frederick I.</p>

<h3><span id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Küstrin_(1535–1571)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-K.C3.BCstrin_.281535.E2.80.931571.29">Margraves of Brandenburg-Küstrin (1535–1571)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Margraves of Brandenburg-Küstrin (1535–1571)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Kuestrin-Kietz.png" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Kuestrin-Kietz.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/33/Wappen_Kuestrin-Kietz.png" width="75" height="94" data-file-width="70" data-file-height="88" /></a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg-K%C3%BCstrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg-Küstrin">Margraviate of Brandenburg-Küstrin</a></div>
<p>The short-lived <a href="/wiki/Margraviate_of_Brandenburg-K%C3%BCstrin" class="mw-redirect" title="Margraviate of Brandenburg-Küstrin">Margraviate of Brandenburg-Küstrin</a> was set up as a <a href="/wiki/Secundogeniture" title="Secundogeniture">secundogeniture</a> of the House of Hohenzollern.</p>
<ul>
<li>1535–1571: <a href="/wiki/John,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-K%C3%BCstrin" title="John, Margrave of Brandenburg-Küstrin">John the Wise</a>, Margrave of Brandenburg-Küstrin (son of <a href="/wiki/Joachim_I_Nestor,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Joachim I Nestor, Elector of Brandenburg">Joachim I Nestor, Elector of Brandenburg</a>. He died without issue. The Margraviate of Brandenburg-Küstrin was absorbed in 1571 into Brandenburg]].</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt_(1688–1788)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt_.281688.E2.80.931788.29">Margraves of Brandenburg-Schwedt (1688–1788)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Margraves of Brandenburg-Schwedt (1688–1788)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Margraves_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt" class="mw-redirect" title="Margraves of Brandenburg-Schwedt">Brandenburg-Schwedt</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Schwedt.png" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Schwedt.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wappen_Schwedt.png/75px-Wappen_Schwedt.png" width="75" height="84" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wappen_Schwedt.png/113px-Wappen_Schwedt.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Wappen_Schwedt.png/150px-Wappen_Schwedt.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="668" /></a></div>
<p>Although recognised as a branch of the dynasty since 1688, the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Schwedt" title="Brandenburg-Schwedt">Margraviate of Brandenburg-Schwedt</a> remained subordinate to the electors, and was never an independent principality.</p>
<ul>
<li>1688–1711: <a href="/wiki/Philip_William,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt" title="Philip William, Margrave of Brandenburg-Schwedt">Philip William</a>, Prince in Prussia, Margrave of Brandenburg-Schwedt (son of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick William, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick William, Elector of Brandenburg</a>)</li>
<li>1731–1771: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt" title="Frederick William, Margrave of Brandenburg-Schwedt">Frederick William</a>, Prince in Prussia, Margrave of Brandenburg-Schwedt (son of)</li>
<li>1771–1788: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Henry,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Schwedt" title="Frederick Henry, Margrave of Brandenburg-Schwedt">Frederick Henry</a>, Prince in Prussia, Margrave of Brandenburg Schwedt (brother of)</li>
</ul>
<h3><span id="Dukes_of_Prussia_(1525–1701)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Dukes_of_Prussia_.281525.E2.80.931701.29">Dukes of Prussia (1525–1701)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Dukes of Prussia (1525–1701)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Prussia" title="List of monarchs of Prussia">Dukes of Prussia</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg" class="image"><img alt="POL Prusy książęce COA.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg/75px-POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg.png" width="75" height="92" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg/113px-POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg/150px-POL_Prusy_ksi%C4%85%C5%BC%C4%99ce_COA.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="734" data-file-height="899" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Acprussiamap2.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Acprussiamap2.gif/400px-Acprussiamap2.gif" width="400" height="280" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/49/Acprussiamap2.gif 1.5x" data-file-width="510" data-file-height="357" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Acprussiamap2.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Growth of <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussia</a>, 1600–1795.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1525 the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Prussia" title="Duchy of Prussia">Duchy of Prussia</a> was established as a <a href="/wiki/Fief" title="Fief">fief</a> of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Polish_monarchs" title="List of Polish monarchs">King of Poland</a>. <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Duke_in_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert, Duke in Prussia">Albert of Prussia</a> was the last <a href="/wiki/Grand_Masters_of_the_Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Grand Masters of the Teutonic Knights">Grand Master</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Teutonic_Knights" class="mw-redirect" title="Teutonic Knights">Teutonic Knights</a> and the first Duke of Prussia. He belonged to the Ansbach branch of the dynasty. The Duchy of Prussia adopted Protestantism as the official <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">state religion</a>.</p>
<ul>
<li>1525–1568: <a href="/wiki/Albert,_Duke_in_Prussia" class="mw-redirect" title="Albert, Duke in Prussia">Albert I</a></li>
<li>1568–1618: <a href="/wiki/Albert_Frederick,_Duke_of_Prussia" title="Albert Frederick, Duke of Prussia">Albert II Frederick</a> co-heir (son of)</li>
<li>1568–1571: <a href="/wiki/Joachim_II_Hector,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Joachim II Hector, Elector of Brandenburg">Joachim I/II Hector</a> co-heir (also Elector of Brandenburg)
<ul>
<li>1578–1603: <a href="/wiki/George_Frederick,_Margrave_of_Brandenburg-Ansbach" title="George Frederick, Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach">George Frederick I/I/I/I</a> (Regent, also Margrave of Brandenburg-Ansbach, Margrave of Brandenburg-Kulmbach and Duke of Brandenburg-Jägerndorf)</li>
<li>1603–1608: <a href="/wiki/Joachim_III_Frederick,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Joachim III Frederick, Elector of Brandenburg">Joachim I/I/III Frederick</a> (Regent, also Duke of Brandenburg-Jägerndorf and Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1608–1618: <a href="/wiki/John_Sigismund,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="John Sigismund, Elector of Brandenburg">John Sigismund</a> (Regent, also Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li>1618–1619: <a href="/wiki/John_Sigismund,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="John Sigismund, Elector of Brandenburg">John Sigismund</a> (Regent, also Elector of Brandenburg, after 1618 <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg-Prussia" title="Brandenburg-Prussia">Brandenburg-Prussia</a>)</li>
<li>1619–1640: <a href="/wiki/George_William,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="George William, Elector of Brandenburg">George William I/I</a> (son of, also Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1640–1688: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William,_Elector_of_Brandenburg" title="Frederick William, Elector of Brandenburg">Frederick I/III William the Great Elector</a> (son of, also Elector of Brandenburg)</li>
<li>1688–1701: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Frederick II/IV/I</a> (also Elector of Brandenburg and King in Prussia)</li>
</ul>
<p>From 1701 the title of Duke of Prussia was attached to the title of King in and of Prussia.</p>
<h3><span id="Kings_in_Prussia_(1701–1772)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kings_in_Prussia_.281701.E2.80.931772.29">Kings in Prussia (1701–1772)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Kings in Prussia (1701–1772)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Preußen.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png/75px-Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png" width="75" height="93" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png/113px-Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png/150px-Wappen_Preu%C3%9Fen.png 2x" data-file-width="483" data-file-height="600" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg/220px-Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg/330px-Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg/440px-Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="409" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Preussen_1701_K%C3%B6nigsberg.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Coronation of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Frederick I</a> in <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigsberg" title="Königsberg">Königsberg</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1701 the title of <a href="/wiki/King_in_Prussia" title="King in Prussia">King in Prussia</a> was granted, without the Duchy of Prussia being elevated to a Kingdom within the Holy Roman Empire. From 1701 onwards the titles of Duke of Prussia and Elector of Brandenburg were always attached to the title of King in Prussia. The Duke of Prussia adopted the title of king as <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick I of Prussia">Frederick I</a>, establishing his status as a monarch whose royal territory lay outside the boundaries of the Holy Roman Empire, with the assent of Emperor <a href="/wiki/Leopold_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Leopold I, Holy Roman Emperor">Leopold I</a>: Frederick could not be "King of Prussia" because part of Prussia's lands were under the <a href="/wiki/Suzerainty" title="Suzerainty">suzerainty</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Kingdom_of_Poland" title="Crown of the Kingdom of Poland">Crown of the Kingdom of Poland</a>. In the age of <a href="/wiki/Absolute_monarchy" title="Absolute monarchy">absolutism</a>, most monarchs were obsessed with the desire to emulate <a href="/wiki/Louis_XIV_of_France" title="Louis XIV of France">Louis XIV of France</a> with his luxurious <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_Versailles" title="Palace of Versailles">palace at Versailles</a>.</p>
<p>In 1772 the Duchy of Prussia was elevated to a kingdom.</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_monarchs_of_Prussia" title="List of monarchs of Prussia">List of monarchs of Prussia</a></div>

<h3><span id="Kings_of_Prussia_(1772–1918)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Kings_of_Prussia_.281772.E2.80.931918.29">Kings of Prussia (1772–1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Kings of Prussia (1772–1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ac.prussiamap3.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ac.prussiamap3.png/300px-Ac.prussiamap3.png" width="300" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ac.prussiamap3.png/450px-Ac.prussiamap3.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Ac.prussiamap3.png/600px-Ac.prussiamap3.png 2x" data-file-width="716" data-file-height="425" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ac.prussiamap3.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Expansion of Prussia 1807–1871</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_I_of_Prussia" title="Frederick William I of Prussia">Frederick William</a>'s successor, <a href="/wiki/Frederick_the_Great" title="Frederick the Great">Frederick the Great</a> gained <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesia</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Silesian_Wars" title="Silesian Wars">Silesian Wars</a> so that Prussia emerged as a <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great power</a>. The king was strongly influenced by French culture and civilization and preferred the French language.</p>
<p>In 1772 the title <i>King of Prussia</i> was assumed. From 1772 onwards the titles of Duke of Prussia and Elector of Brandenburg were always attached to the title King of Prussia.</p>
<p>In 1871 the Kingdom of Prussia became a constituent member of the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a>.</p>

<h3><span id="German_Emperors_(1871–1918)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="German_Emperors_.281871.E2.80.931918.29">German Emperors (1871–1918)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: German Emperors (1871–1918)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/German_Emperor" title="German Emperor">German Emperor</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png" class="image"><img alt="Hohenzollern Reichswappen Kleines.png" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png/75px-Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png" width="75" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png/113px-Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png/150px-Hohenzollern_Reichswappen_Kleines.png 2x" data-file-width="240" data-file-height="288" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Prussiamap.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Prussiamap.gif/330px-Prussiamap.gif" width="330" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Prussiamap.gif/495px-Prussiamap.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e7/Prussiamap.gif 2x" data-file-width="577" data-file-height="415" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Prussiamap.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Prussia in the German Empire 1871–1918</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1871 the German Empire was proclaimed. With the accession of <a href="/wiki/William_I,_German_Emperor" title="William I, German Emperor">William I</a> to the newly established imperial German throne, the titles of King of Prussia, Duke of Prussia and Elector of Brandenburg were always attached to the title of <a href="/wiki/German_Emperor" title="German Emperor">German Emperor</a>.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Minister_President_of_Prussia" title="Minister President of Prussia">Prussia's Minister President</a> <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Otto von Bismarck</a> convinced William that German Emperor instead of Emperor of Germany would be appropriate. He became <i><a href="/wiki/Primus_inter_pares" title="Primus inter pares">primus inter pares</a></i> among other German sovereigns.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II,_German_Emperor" title="Wilhelm II, German Emperor">William II</a> intended to develop a <a href="/wiki/Imperial_German_Navy" title="Imperial German Navy">German navy</a> capable of challenging Britain's <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">Royal Navy</a>. The assassination of <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria</a> on 28 June 1914 set off the chain of events that led to <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>. As a result of the war, the German, Russian, Austro-Hungarian and Ottoman empires ceased to exist.</p>
<p>In 1918 the German empire was abolished and replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a>. After the outbreak of the German revolution in 1918, both Emperor Wilhelm II and Crown Prince <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm,_German_Crown_Prince" title="Wilhelm, German Crown Prince">Wilhelm</a> signed the document of abdication.</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Brandenburg-Prussian_branch_since_1918_abdication">Brandenburg-Prussian branch since 1918 abdication</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Brandenburg-Prussian branch since 1918 abdication">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_(1201)b.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg/170px-2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg" width="170" height="308" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg/255px-2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg/340px-2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_%281201%29b.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1811" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2017-07-08_Wedding_Ekaterina_Malysheva_und_Ernst_August_von_Hannover_(1201)b.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Georg Friedrich, the head of the Prussian Hohenzollerns and his wife</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In June 1926, a <a href="/wiki/Expropriation_of_the_Princes_in_the_Weimar_Republic" title="Expropriation of the Princes in the Weimar Republic">referendum on expropriating the formerly ruling princes of Germany</a> without compensation failed and as a consequence, the financial situation of the Hohenzollern family improved considerably. A settlement between the state and the family made <a href="/wiki/Cecilienhof" title="Cecilienhof">Cecilienhof</a> property of the state but granted a right of residence to Crown Prince Wilhelm and his wife Cecilie. The family also kept the ownership of <a href="/wiki/Monbijou_Palace" title="Monbijou Palace">Monbijou Palace</a> in Berlin, <a href="/wiki/Ole%C5%9Bnica_Castle" title="Oleśnica Castle">Oleśnica Castle</a> in Silesia, <a href="/wiki/Rheinsberg_Palace" title="Rheinsberg Palace">Rheinsberg Palace</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schwedt" title="Schwedt">Schwedt</a> Palace and other property until 1945.</p>
<p>Since the abolition of the German monarchy, no Hohenzollern claims to imperial or royal prerogatives are recognised by Germany's <a href="/wiki/Basic_Law_for_the_Federal_Republic_of_Germany" title="Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany">Basic Law for the Federal Republic of Germany</a> of 1949, which guarantees a republic.</p>
<p>The communist government of the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_zone" title="Soviet occupation zone">Soviet occupation zone</a> depropriated all landowners and industrialists; the House of Hohenzollern lost almost all of its fortune, retaining a few company shares and <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a>. The Polish government appropriated the <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">Silesian</a> property and the Dutch government seized <a href="/wiki/Huis_Doorn" title="Huis Doorn">Huis Doorn</a>, the Emperor's seat in exile.</p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> however, the family was legally able to re-claim their portable property, namely art collections and parts of the interior of their former palaces. Negotiations on the return of or compensation for these assets are not yet completed.</p>
<p>Berlin's <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Palace" title="Berlin Palace">old City Palace</a> is being rebuilt and is scheduled to open in 2019. The Berlin Palace and the <a href="/wiki/Humboldt_Forum" title="Humboldt Forum">Humboldt Forum</a> are located in the middle of Berlin.</p>

<th scope="row">Carl Friedrich, Prince of Prussia</th>
<td></td>
<td>Son of (<a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The head of the house is the titular King of Prussia and German Emperor. He also bears a historical claim to the title of <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Orange" title="Prince of Orange">Prince of Orange</a>. Members of this line style themselves princes of Prussia.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Georg_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Prussia" title="Georg Friedrich, Prince of Prussia">Georg Friedrich, Prince of Prussia</a>, the current head of the royal Prussian House of Hohenzollern, was married to <a href="/wiki/Princess_Sophie_of_Isenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Princess Sophie of Isenburg">Princess Sophie of Isenburg</a> on 27 August 2011. On 20 January 2013, she gave birth to twin sons, Carl Friedrich Franz Alexander and Louis Ferdinand Christian Albrecht, in <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a>. Carl Friedrich, the elder of the two, is the heir apparent.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_House_of_Hohenzollern_table">Royal House of Hohenzollern table</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Royal House of Hohenzollern table">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:702px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg/700px-Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg.png" width="700" height="991" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg/1050px-Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e4/Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg/1400px-Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1704" data-file-height="2413" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Genealogy_of_House_of_Hohenzollern.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Table of the Royal Brandenburg-Prussian House of Hohenzollern</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Swabian_branch">Swabian branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Swabian branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg/220px-Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg" width="220" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg/330px-Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg/440px-Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1339" data-file-height="1401" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Schloss_Sigmaringen_Wappen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Combined coat of arms of the House of <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> (1849).</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The senior Swabian<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated178_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated178-7">[7]</a></sup> branch of the House of Hohenzollern was founded by <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick IV, Count of Zollern">Frederick IV, Count of Zollern</a>. The family ruled three territories with seats at, respectively, <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Hechingen" title="Hohenzollern-Hechingen">Hechingen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Sigmaringen</a> and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Haigerloch</a>. The counts were elevated to princes in 1623. The Swabian branch of the Hohenzollerns was <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a>.</p>
<p>Affected by economic problems and internal feuds, the Hohenzollern counts from the 14th century onwards came under pressure by their neighbors, the Counts of <a href="/wiki/W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Württemberg">Württemberg</a> and the cities of the <a href="/wiki/Swabian_League" title="Swabian League">Swabian League</a>, whose troops besieged and finally destroyed Hohenzollern Castle in 1423. Nevertheless, the Hohenzollerns retained their estates, backed by their Brandenburg cousins and the Imperial <a href="/wiki/House_of_Habsburg" title="House of Habsburg">House of Habsburg</a>. In 1535, Count <a href="/wiki/Karl_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl I, Count of Hohenzollern">Charles I of Hohenzollern</a> (1512–1576) received the counties of <a href="/wiki/Sigmaringen#History" title="Sigmaringen">Sigmaringen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Veringenstadt" title="Veringenstadt">Veringen</a> as Imperial fiefs.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1576, when <a href="/wiki/Karl_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl I, Count of Hohenzollern">Charles I, Count of Hohenzollern</a> died, his county was divided to form the three Swabian branches. <a href="/wiki/Eitel_Friedrich_IV,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Eitel Friedrich IV, Count of Hohenzollern">Eitel Frederick IV</a> took <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern</a> with the title of Hohenzollern-Hechingen, <a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Charles II, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Karl II</a> took Sigmaringen and Veringen, and <a href="/wiki/Christoph,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Christoph, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Christopher</a> got Haigerloch. Christopher's family died out in 1634.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Eitel_Friedrich_IV,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Eitel Friedrich IV, Count of Hohenzollern">Eitel Frederick IV of Hohenzollern-Hechingen</a> (1545–1605)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Charles_II,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Charles II, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Charles II of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> (1547–1606)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Christoph,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Christoph, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Christopher of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch</a> (1552–1592)</li>
</ul>
<p>In 1695, the remaining two Swabian branches entered into an agreement with the Margrave of Brandenburg which provided that if both branches became extinct, the principalities should fall to Brandenburg. Because of the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, <a href="/wiki/Constantine,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern-Hechingen" title="Constantine, Prince of Hohenzollern-Hechingen">Constantine</a>, Prince of Hohenzollern-Hechingen and <a href="/wiki/Karl_Anton,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Anton, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Anton</a>, Prince of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen abdicated their thrones in December 1849. The principalities were ruled by the Kings of Prussia from December 1849 onward, with the Hechingen and Sigmaringen branches obtaining official treatment as cadets of the Prussian royal family.</p>
<p>The Hohenzollern-Hechingen branch became extinct in 1869. A descendent of this branch was <a href="/wiki/Sophie,_Duchess_of_Hohenberg" title="Sophie, Duchess of Hohenberg">Countess Sophie Chotek</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morganatic_marriage" title="Morganatic marriage">morganatic wife</a> of <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria-Este</a>.</p>

</div>
</div>

</ul>
<h3><span id="Counts_of_Hohenzollern_(1204–1575)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Counts_of_Hohenzollern_.281204.E2.80.931575.29">Counts of Hohenzollern (1204–1575)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Counts of Hohenzollern (1204–1575)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg/75px-Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg" width="75" height="80" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg/113px-Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg/150px-Hohenzollern-herb-rodowy.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="638" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_(1871).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg/220px-German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg.png" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg/330px-German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg/440px-German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_%281871%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="976" data-file-height="818" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:German_Empire_-_Prussia_-_Hohenzollern_(1871).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hohenzollern region, in present-day <a href="/wiki/Baden-W%C3%BCrttemberg" title="Baden-Württemberg">Baden-Württemberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> (red color)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1204, the County of Hohenzollern was established out of the fusion of the County of Zollern and the <a href="/wiki/Burgraviate_of_Nuremberg" title="Burgraviate of Nuremberg">Burgraviate of Nuremberg</a>. The Swabian branch inherited the county of Zollern and, being descended from Frederick I of Nuremberg, were all named "Friedrich" down through the 11th generation.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup> Each one's numeral is counted from the first Friedrich to rule his branch's <a href="/wiki/Appanage" title="Appanage">appanage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The most senior of these in the 12th century, Count <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VIII,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick VIII, Count of Zollern">Frederick VIII</a> (d. 1333), had two sons, the elder of whom became <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IX,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick IX, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick IX</a> (d. 1379), first Count of Hohenzollern, and fathered Friedrich X who left no sons when he died in 1412.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>But the younger son of Friedrich VIII, called <i>Friedrich of Strassburg</i>, uniquely, took no numeral of his own, retaining the old title "Count of Zollern" and pre-deceased his brother in 1364/65.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup> Prince Wilhelm Karl zu Isenburg's 1957 genealogical series, <i><a href="/wiki/Europ%C3%A4ische_Stammtafeln" title="Europäische Stammtafeln">Europäische Stammtafeln</a></i>, says Friedrich of Strassburg shared, rather, in the rule of Zollern with his elder brother until his premature death.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>It appears, but is not stated, that Strassburg's son became the recognized co-ruler of his cousin Friedrich X (as compensation for having received no appanage and/or because of incapacity on the part of Friedrich X) and, as such, assumed (or is, historically, attributed) the designation <a href="/wiki/Frederick_XI,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick XI, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick XI</a> although he actually pre-deceased Friedrich X, dying in 1401.</p>
<p>Friedrich XI, however, left two sons who jointly succeeded their cousin-once-removed, being Count <a href="/wiki/Frederick_XII,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick XII, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick XII</a> (d. childless 1443) and Count Eitel Friedrich I (d. 1439), the latter becoming the ancestor of all subsequent branches of the Princes of Hohenzollern.<sup id="cite_ref-huberty_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huberty-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>1204–1251/1255: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IV,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick IV, Count of Zollern">Frederick IV</a>, also Burgrave of Nuremberg as Frederick II until 1218</li>
<li>1251/1255–1289: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_V,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick V, Count of Zollern">Frederick V</a></li>
<li>1289–1298: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VI,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick VI, Count of Zollern">Frederick VI</a> (d. 1298), son of</li>
<li>1298–1309: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VII,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick VII, Count of Zollern">Frederick VII</a> (d. after 1309), son of</li>
<li>1309–1333: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_VIII,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick VIII, Count of Zollern">Frederick VIII</a> (d. 1333), brother of</li>
<li>1333–1377: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_IX,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick IX, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick IX</a></li>
<li>1377–1401: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_XI,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick XI, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick XI</a></li>
<li>1401–1426: <a href="/wiki/Frederick_XII,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick XII, Count of Hohenzollern">Frederick XII</a></li>
<li>1426–1439: <a href="/w/index.php?title=Eitel_Frederick_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Eitel Frederick I, Count of Hohenzollern (page does not exist)">Eitel Frederick I</a>, brother of</li>
<li>1433–1488: <a href="/wiki/Jobst_Nikolaus_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Jobst Nikolaus I, Count of Hohenzollern">Jobst Nicholas I</a> (1433–1488), son of</li>
<li>1488–1512: <a href="/wiki/Eitel_Friedrich_II,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Eitel Friedrich II, Count of Hohenzollern">Eitel Frederick II</a> (c. 1452–1512), son of</li>
<li>1512–1525: <a href="/wiki/Eitel_Friedrich_III,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Eitel Friedrich III, Count of Hohenzollern">Eitel Frederick III</a> (1494–1525), son of</li>
<li>1525–1575: <a href="/wiki/Karl_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl I, Count of Hohenzollern">Charles I</a> (1516–1576), son of</li>
</ul>
<p>In the 12th century, a son of <a href="/wiki/Frederick_I,_Count_of_Zollern" title="Frederick I, Count of Zollern">Frederick I</a> secured the county of <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Hohenberg" title="Count of Hohenberg">Hohenberg</a>. The county remained in the possession of the family until 1486.</p>
<p>The influence of the Swabian line was weakened by several partitions of its lands. In the 16th century, the situation changed completely when <a href="/wiki/Eitel_Friedrich_II,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Eitel Friedrich II, Count of Hohenzollern">Eitel Frederick II</a>, a friend and adviser of the emperor <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Maximilian I</a>, received the district of <a href="/wiki/Haigerloch" title="Haigerloch">Haigerloch</a>. His grandson <a href="/wiki/Karl_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl I, Count of Hohenzollern">Charles I</a> was granted the counties of Sigmaringen and Vehringen by <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V</a>.</p>
<h3><span id="Counts,_later_Princes_of_Hohenzollern-Hechingen_(1576–1849)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Counts.2C_later_Princes_of_Hohenzollern-Hechingen_.281576.E2.80.931849.29">Counts, later Princes of Hohenzollern-Hechingen (1576–1849)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Counts, later Princes of Hohenzollern-Hechingen (1576–1849)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Hechingen" title="Hohenzollern-Hechingen">Hohenzollern-Hechingen</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG" class="image"><img alt="Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG/75px-Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG" width="75" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG/113px-Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG/150px-Hohenzollern-Hechingen-1.PNG 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="714" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Klosterkirche_Stetten_(Hechingen).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG/220px-Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG/330px-Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG/440px-Klosterkirche_Stetten_%28Hechingen%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Klosterkirche_Stetten_(Hechingen).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Stetten Abbey church in <a href="/wiki/Hechingen" title="Hechingen">Hechingen</a>, the burial place of the Swabian line</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Hechingen" title="Hohenzollern-Hechingen">County of Hohenzollern-Hechingen</a> was established in 1576 with <a href="/wiki/Allodial" class="mw-redirect" title="Allodial">allodial</a> rights. It included the original County of Zollern, with the <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern_Castle" title="Hohenzollern Castle">Hohenzollern Castle</a> and the monastery at Stetten.</p>
<p>In December 1849, the ruling princes of both Hohenzollern-Hechingen and Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen abdicated their thrones, and their principalities were incorporated as the Prussian <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Hohenzollern" title="Province of Hohenzollern">province of Hohenzollern</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup> The Hechingen branch became extinct in dynastic line with Konstantin's death in 1869.</p>
