<h3><span id="Counts_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch_(1576–1634_and_1681–1767)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Counts_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch_.281576.E2.80.931634_and_1681.E2.80.931767.29">Counts of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch (1576–1634 and 1681–1767)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Counts of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch (1576–1634 and 1681–1767)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Hohenzollern-Haigerloch</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Wappen_Haigerloch.svg" class="image"><img alt="Wappen Haigerloch.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Wappen_Haigerloch.svg/75px-Wappen_Haigerloch.svg.png" width="75" height="77" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Wappen_Haigerloch.svg/113px-Wappen_Haigerloch.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Wappen_Haigerloch.svg/150px-Wappen_Haigerloch.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="613" /></a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">County of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch</a> was established in 1576 without allodial rights.</p>
<ul>
<li>1576–1601&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Christoph,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Christoph, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Christopher</a> (1552–1592), son of <a href="/wiki/Karl_I,_Count_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl I, Count of Hohenzollern">Charles I of Hohenzollern</a></li>
<li>1601–1623&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Johann_Christoph,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Johann Christoph, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">John Christopher</a> (1586–1620), son of</li>
<li>1601–1634&#160;: <a href="/wiki/Charles,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Charles, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Charles</a> (1588–1634)</li>
</ul>
<p>Between 1634 and 1681, the county was temporarily integrated into the principality of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.</p>
<ul>
<li>1681–1702: <a href="/wiki/Franz_Anton,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Haigerloch" title="Franz Anton, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch">Francis Anthony, Count of Hohenzollern-Haigerloch</a></li>
<li>1702–1750: <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Leopold,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Ferdinand Leopold, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Ferdinand Leopold, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a></li>
<li>1750–1767: <a href="/wiki/Franz_Christoph_Anton,_Count_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Franz Christoph Anton, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Francis Christopher Anton, Count of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Upon the death of Francis Christopher Anton in 1767, the Haigerloch territory was incorporated into the principality of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.</p>
<h3><span id="Counts,_later_Princes_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen_(1576–1849)"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Counts.2C_later_Princes_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen_.281576.E2.80.931849.29">Counts, later Princes of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen (1576–1849)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Counts, later Princes of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen (1576–1849)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a></div>
<div class="floatright"><a href="/wiki/File:Hohenzollern-2.PNG" class="image"><img alt="Hohenzollern-2.PNG" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hohenzollern-2.PNG/75px-Hohenzollern-2.PNG" width="75" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hohenzollern-2.PNG/113px-Hohenzollern-2.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/Hohenzollern-2.PNG/150px-Hohenzollern-2.PNG 2x" data-file-width="594" data-file-height="711" /></a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg/220px-Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg/330px-Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg/440px-Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3660" data-file-height="2423" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sigmaringen_Schloss_BW_2015-04-28_17-37-14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Sigmaringen Castle</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The County of <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> was established in 1576 with allodial rights and a seat at <a href="/wiki/Sigmaringen_Castle" title="Sigmaringen Castle">Sigmaringen Castle</a>.</p>
<p>In December 1849, sovereignty over the principality was yielded to the Franconian branch of the family and incorporated into the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Prussia" title="Kingdom of Prussia">Kingdom of Prussia</a>, which accorded status as cadets of the Prussian Royal Family to the Swabian Hohenzollerns. The last ruling Prince of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen, <a href="/wiki/Karl_Anton,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Anton, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Anton</a>, would later serve as <a href="/wiki/Minister_President_of_Prussia" title="Minister President of Prussia">Minister President of Prussia</a> between 1858 and 1862.</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen_after_1849">House of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen after 1849</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: House of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen after 1849">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen" title="Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen">House of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:332px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte-Hohenzollern.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Karte-Hohenzollern.png/330px-Karte-Hohenzollern.png" width="330" height="253" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Karte-Hohenzollern.png/495px-Karte-Hohenzollern.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Karte-Hohenzollern.png/660px-Karte-Hohenzollern.png 2x" data-file-width="1274" data-file-height="977" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Karte-Hohenzollern.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Map of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Hohenzollern" title="Province of Hohenzollern">Province of Hohenzollern</a>, a de facto province of Prussia after 1850.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Graf_von_dem_Bergh,_F%C3%BCrst_Karl_Friedrich_von_Hohenzollern,_Chef_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Graf_von_dem_Bergh%2C_F%C3%BCrst_Karl_Friedrich_von_Hohenzollern%2C_Chef_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.jpg/220px-Graf_von_dem_Bergh%2C_F%C3%BCrst_Karl_Friedrich_von_Hohenzollern%2C_Chef_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.jpg" width="220" height="188" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/56/Graf_von_dem_Bergh%2C_F%C3%BCrst_Karl_Friedrich_von_Hohenzollern%2C_Chef_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="317" data-file-height="271" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graf_von_dem_Bergh,_F%C3%BCrst_Karl_Friedrich_von_Hohenzollern,_Chef_Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern</a>, head of the Swabian branch</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The family continued to use the title of Prince of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen. After the Hechingen branch became extinct in 1869, the Sigmaringen branch adopted title of <i>Prince of Hohenzollern</i>.</p>
<ul>
<li>1849–1885: <a href="/wiki/Karl_Anton,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Anton, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Anton</a></li>
<li>1885–1905: <a href="/wiki/Leopold,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Leopold, Prince of Hohenzollern">Leopold</a> (1835–1905), son of</li>
<li>1905–1927: <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" class="mw-redirect" title="Wilhelm, Prince of Hohenzollern">William</a> (1864–1927), son of</li>
<li>1927–1965: <a href="/wiki/Frederick,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Frederick, Prince of Hohenzollern">Frederick</a> (1891–1965), son of</li>
<li>1965–2010: <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Wilhelm,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Friedrich Wilhelm, Prince of Hohenzollern">Friedrich Wilhelm</a> (1924–2010), son of</li>
<li>2010–present: <a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Friedrich</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a>: <a href="/wiki/Alexander,_Hereditary_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Alexander, Hereditary Prince of Hohenzollern">Alexander</a></li>
</ul>
<p>In 1866, <a href="/wiki/Carol_I_of_Romania" title="Carol I of Romania">Prince Charles</a> of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen was chosen <a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" title="United Principalities">prince of Rumania</a>, becoming <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romanians" title="King of the Romanians">King</a> Carol I of Romania in 1881.</p>
<p>Charles's elder brother, <a href="/wiki/Leopold,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Leopold, Prince of Hohenzollern">Leopold, Prince of Hohenzollern</a>, was offered the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Spain" title="Monarchy of Spain">Spanish throne</a> after a revolt exiled <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Isabella II</a> in 1870. Although encouraged by <a href="/wiki/Otto_von_Bismarck" title="Otto von Bismarck">Bismarck</a> to accept, Leopold declined in the face of French opposition. Nonetheless, Bismarck altered and then published the <a href="/wiki/Ems_Dispatch" title="Ems Dispatch">Ems telegram</a> to create a <i><a href="/wiki/Casus_belli" title="Casus belli">casus belli</a></i>: France declared war, but Bismarck's Germany won the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a>.</p>
<p>The head of the Sigmaringen branch (the only extant line of the Swabian branch of the dynasty) is <a href="/wiki/Karl_Friedrich,_Prince_of_Hohenzollern" title="Karl Friedrich, Prince of Hohenzollern">Karl Friedrich</a>, styled <i>His Serene Highness</i> The Prince of Hohenzollern. His official seat is <a href="/wiki/Sigmaringen_Castle" title="Sigmaringen Castle">Sigmaringen Castle</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ghda_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ghda-2">[2]</a></sup></p>

</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Principalities" title="United Principalities">Principality of Romania</a> was established in 1862, after the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman</a> vassal states of <a href="/wiki/Wallachia" title="Wallachia">Wallachia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moldavia" title="Moldavia">Moldavia</a> had been united in 1859 under <a href="/wiki/Alexandru_Ioan_Cuza" title="Alexandru Ioan Cuza">Alexandru Ioan Cuza</a> as <a href="/wiki/Domnitor" title="Domnitor">Prince of Romania</a> in a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>. He was deposed in 1866 by the Romanian parliament.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Carol_I_of_Romania" title="Carol I of Romania">Prince Charles of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a> was invited to become reigning Prince of Romania in 1866. In 1881 he became Carol I, <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romanians" title="King of the Romanians">King of the Romanians</a>. Carol I had an only daughter who died young, so the younger son of his brother Leopold, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_I_of_Romania" title="Ferdinand I of Romania">Prince Ferdinand of Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen</a>, would succeed his uncle as King of the Romanians in 1914, and his descendants, having converted to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Orthodox Church</a>, continued to reign there until the end of the monarchy in 1947.</p>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/King_of_the_Romanians" title="King of the Romanians">King of the Romanians</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanian_royal_family" title="Romanian royal family">Romanian royal family</a></div>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Succession_since_1947">Succession since 1947</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Succession since 1947">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Line_of_succession_to_the_former_Romanian_throne" title="Line of succession to the former Romanian throne">Line of succession to the former Romanian throne</a></div>
<p>In 1947 the Kingdom of Romania was abolished and replaced with the <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Republic_of_Romania" title="Socialist Republic of Romania">People's Republic of Romania</a>. <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael</a> does not press his claim to the defunct Romanian throne and although he has been welcomed back to the country after half a century in exile as a private citizen, with substantial former royal properties being placed at his disposal. However, his dynastic claim is not recognised by post-Communist Romanians.</p>
<p>On 10 May 2011, Michael severed the dynastic ties between the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Romania" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Romania">House of Romania</a> and the House of Hohenzollern.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> The branch of the Hohenzollerns is now <a href="/wiki/Dynasty#Dynasts" title="Dynasty">dynastically</a> represented only by the last king <a href="/wiki/Michael_I_of_Romania" title="Michael I of Romania">Michael of Romania</a>, and his daughters. Having no sons, he declared that his dynastic heir, instead of being a male member of the Hohenzollern-Sigmaringen princely family to which he belongs <a href="/wiki/Patrilineality" title="Patrilineality">patrilineally</a> and in accordance with the last Romanian monarchical constitution, shall be his eldest daughter <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margareta_of_Romania" title="Princess Margareta of Romania">Margareta</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The royal house is still very popular<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> and in 2014 Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Victor_Ponta" title="Victor Ponta">Victor Ponta</a> promised a referendum on whether or not to reinstate the monarchy if he were re-elected.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Palaces_of_the_Prussian_Hohenzollerns">Palaces of the Prussian Hohenzollerns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Hohenzollern&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Palaces of the Prussian Hohenzollerns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
